  called out once code exists)

        5  ## What This Project Is
        6  
        5 -AgentWatch is an AI observability platform that gives enterpri
          -se security teams a single pane of glass for all AI agent acti
          -vity. It correlates endpoint state, agent identity, tool invoc
          -ations, and model interactions regardless of which AI client (
          -VS Code/Copilot, Cursor, Claude Code, Codex CLI), model provid
          -er (OpenAI, Anthropic, Google), or tool ecosystem (MCP servers
          -, function calling) is in use.                                
        7 +AgentWatch is an AI observability platform for enterprise secu
          +rity teams. It correlates telemetry from three planes вҖ” extern
          +al API calls, internal network (MCP servers), and local endpoi
          +nt (processes, config files) вҖ” to give unified visibility into
          + AI agent activity across all clients (VS Code/Copilot, Cursor
          +, Claude Code, Codex CLI) and providers (OpenAI, Anthropic, Go
          +ogle).

          + вҖ” zero latency impact, no conflict with existing SASE/proxy i
          +nfrastructure.                                                
       10  
        9 -**Core insight:** AI activity happens across three planes вҖ” ex
          -ternal API calls, internal network (MCP servers, databases), a
          -nd local endpoint (process-to-process stdio, config files). No
          - existing tool sees all three. SASE tools like Zscaler only se
          -e external API calls. MCP gateways only see MCP protocol traff
          -ic. AgentWatch correlates telemetry from all three planes.

       35  ### Four Telemetry Collectors
       36 +1. **Endpoint Agent** вҖ” Scans AI client MCP config paths, runn
          +ing processes, network listeners. PowerShell (Windows), Python
          + (macOS/Linux). Deployed via Intune/GPO.                      
       37 +2. **Orchestrator Hooks** вҖ” Agent/user identity, tool invocati
          +ons, command validation, session context.

          +tHub Copilot admin APIs.                                      
       39 +4. **Network Telemetry** вҖ” Ingests Zscaler ZIA, firewall, DNS 
          +logs. Note: Zscaler bypasses internal traffic, which is why co
          +llectors 1 and 2 are critical.

       41  ### Correlation Engine
       68 -Joins telemetry from all four collectors using shared keys: us
          -ername, hostname, timestamp window, agent identity. Produces c
          -orrelated events like shadow agent detection, credential expos
          -ure, behavioral anomalies.                                    
       42 +Joins across collectors using: username, hostname, timestamp w
          +indow, agent identity.                                        
       43  
       70 -### Safety LLM                                                
       71 -Async evaluation service (Claude Haiku) that reviews agent ses
          -sions for behavioral patterns rule-based detection misses. Run
          -s on completed/in-progress sessions вҖ” does NOT add latency. Fo
          -r time-critical agents (SecOps, trading), static policy checks
          - at the orchestrator provide real-time enforcement.           
       44 +### Three-Lane Enforcement                                    
       45 +- **Fast lane:** Registered + approved вҶ’ microsecond policy ch
          +eck, no LLM.                                                  
       46 +- **Inspection lane:** Unregistered/new вҶ’ full Safety LLM eval
          +uation.                                                       
       47 +- **Blocked lane:** Explicitly denied вҶ’ instant static block. 
       48  
       73 -### Three-Lane Enforcement Model                              
       74 -- **Fast lane:** Registered + approved agents. Microsecond pol
          -icy check against registry. No LLM evaluation.                
       75 -- **Inspection lane:** Unregistered or new agents. Full safety
          - LLM evaluation.                                              
       76 -- **Blocked lane:** Explicitly denied actions. Instant static 
          -block.                                                        
       49 +### Agent Identity Model                                      
       50 +Every agent has: registered identity (unique ID in registry), 
          +delegation chain (agent + human identity), scoped permissions 
          +(infrastructure-enforced), ephemeral JWT credential (per-sessi
          +on), full traceability (agent ID + user ID + session ID on eve
          +ry log entry).

       82 -1. **Registered Identity** вҖ” exists in registry before it can

       83 -2. **Delegation Chain** вҖ” acts on behalf of a human. Both iden
          -tities logged. Format: "DLP Agent (agent:dlp-001) acting for m

          -D, user ID, session ID.

      108 -## Known Issues in Existing Code                              
      109 -                                                              
      110 -1. **No user identity in logs.** Every log entry records agent
          - and command but NOT who ran it. Critical gap.                
      111 -2. **No API authentication.** Anyone on the network who can re
          -ach port 3000 can execute commands. Must add JWT or API key va
          -lidation.                                                     
      112 -3. **Validation regex false positive.** Pattern `[A-Z][a-z]+-[
          -A-Za-z]+` catches string literals like `"=== ACTIVE Global Adm
          -ins ==="` inside commands. Fix: strip quoted strings before va
          -lidation.                                                     
      113 -4. **CopilotBridge is voluntary.** If a developer doesn't Impo
          -rt-Module, their activity is invisible. This is the shadow age
          -nt problem.                                                   
      114 -5. **AGENTS object is hardcoded.** Must externalize to databas
          -e/config with CRUD API.                                       
      115 -6. **Invoke-Expression in CopilotBridge.** Security risk (exec
          -utes arbitrary strings). Mitigated by blocked verb list but fl
          -agged in reviews.                                             
      116 -7. **In-memory history.** History array resets on restart. Mus
          -t persist to database.

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Based on your background (Python comfortable, not a heavy coder, building
      a security product), here's my recommendation. Python-to-Go migration is 
     essentially a full rewrite вҖ” not a migration. BUT: you don't need Go yet. 
     FastAPI (Python) gives you production-grade async API, WebSocket support, 
     auto-generated API docs, and SQLAlchemy ORM. Same language for API + 
     endpoint agent = one codebase to learn and maintain. Performance won't 
     matter until hundreds of endpoints are reporting. If you outgrow Python, 
     you'll have a working product with clear API contracts to rewrite from. Go 
     with Python for everything? вҶ’ Yes, Python everywhere (Recommended)

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· You're right that cloud-hosted AI activity is a gap. But here's the 
     thing: the endpoint agent we're building in Python is already 
     cross-platform вҖ” it can run on cloud VMs, Codespaces, EC2 instances just 
     the same. The bigger cloud gap is collecting from cloud-native sources 
     (CloudTrail for AI API calls, Azure Activity Logs, GCP audit logs, GitHub 
     Actions AI usage). That's essentially Collector 3 + 4 from the 
     architecture. My recommendation: ship the core platform first (API, 
     dashboard, agent, Helm chart), then add cloud collectors as integrations. 
     The architecture already has slots for them. Trying to build cloud 
     integrations before the core platform exists means we have nothing to 
     collect INTO. Make sense to continue with the core build now? вҶ’ Yes, core 
     first, cloud later (Recommended)

  вҺҝ В Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/snuggly-scribbling-toucan.md В· /plan to edit
     AgentWatch Platform Build Plan

     Context

     Building the AgentWatch AI observability platform from scratch as a
     cross-platform, production-ready application. The platform needs to work on
      Mac, Windows, and Linux. The UI/reporting runs in Kubernetes via Helm
     chart. All backend code in Python, dashboard in React + Tailwind.

     Decisions Made

     - API/Orchestrator: Python (FastAPI) with async SQLAlchemy + PostgreSQL
     - Endpoint Agent: Python (cross-platform, single codebase)
     - Dashboard: React + Tailwind, bundled with API as static files
     - Local Dev: Docker Compose
     - Deployment: Helm chart for Kubernetes

     ---
     Project Structure

     agentwatch/
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ docker-compose.yml           # Local dev stack
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ Makefile                     # Build/dev commands
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ .env.example                 # Env var template
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ .gitignore
     в”Ӯ
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ orchestrator/                # FastAPI API + serves dashboard
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ Dockerfile
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pyproject.toml
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ alembic.ini
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ alembic/                 # DB migrations
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ app/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ main.py              # FastAPI app, CORS, lifespan
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.py            # Pydantic Settings from env
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ database.py          # Async SQLAlchemy engine/session
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ auth.py              # JWT + API key middleware
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ models/              # SQLAlchemy ORM models
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ schemas/             # Pydantic request/response
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ routers/             # API route handlers
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ services/            # Business logic
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tests/
     в”Ӯ
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ agent/                       # Endpoint scanner agent
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ Dockerfile
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ pyproject.toml
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ agentwatch_agent/
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cli.py               # Typer CLI entry point
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ scanners/            # Config, process, network scanners
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ reporters/           # API + file reporters
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ scoring.py           # Risk scoring engine
     в”Ӯ   в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ platforms/           # OS-specific path resolution
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tests/
     в”Ӯ
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ dashboard/                   # React + Tailwind
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ package.json
     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ vite.config.ts
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ src/                     # Components, hooks, API client
     в”Ӯ
     в”ңв”Җв”Җ helm/
     в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ agentwatch/              # Helm chart
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ Chart.yaml
     в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ values.yaml
     в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ templates/           # K8s manifests
     в”Ӯ
     в””в”Җв”Җ agent-instructions/          # Agent definition markdown files

     ---
     Implementation Phases (this session)

     Phase A: Scaffolding

     1. Create project structure, .gitignore, Makefile, .env.example
     2. Set up orchestrator pyproject.toml (FastAPI, SQLAlchemy, alembic, PyJWT,
      uvicorn, asyncpg)
     3. Set up agent pyproject.toml (typer, psutil, httpx, rich)
     4. Set up dashboard package.json (React, Vite, Tailwind, TypeScript)

     Phase B: Orchestrator API

     1. app/config.py вҖ” Pydantic Settings (DB URL, JWT secret, API port, log
     path)
     2. app/database.py вҖ” Async SQLAlchemy engine, session factory, Base
     3. app/models/ вҖ” SQLAlchemy models:
       - agent.py: Agent registry (id, name, type, owner, status, permissions,
     api_key_hash, timestamps)
       - audit_log.py: Audit entries (id, agent_id, user_id, session_id, action,
      command, result, risk_level, timestamp)
       - user.py: Users (id, username, email, password_hash, role, timestamps)
       - scan_result.py: Endpoint scan results (id, hostname, findings,
     risk_summary, timestamp)
     4. app/schemas/ вҖ” Pydantic v2 models for all request/response shapes
     5. app/auth.py вҖ” JWT creation/validation, API key validation, auth
     dependency
     6. app/services/validator.py вҖ” Command validation with quoted-string
     stripping (fixes known issue #3)
     7. app/services/orchestrator.py вҖ” Prompt routing via keyword scoring, agent
      selection
     8. app/services/audit_logger.py вҖ” Dual logging: JSONL files + PostgreSQL
     9. app/routers/:
       - auth.py: POST /api/auth/login, POST /api/auth/register
       - agents.py: CRUD for agent registry
       - audit.py: POST /api/prompt, /api/validate, /api/execute, GET
     /api/history, /api/stats
       - reports.py: POST /api/report (endpoint agent reports)
       - ws.py: WebSocket /ws/feed for real-time dashboard
       - health.py: GET /api/health (unauthenticated)
     10. app/main.py вҖ” FastAPI app with lifespan, middleware, static file
     serving
     11. Alembic setup + initial migration
     12. Tests for auth, validator, orchestrator logic

     Phase C: Endpoint Agent

     1. platforms/ вҖ” OS-specific MCP config path resolution (Windows, macOS,
     Linux)
     2. scanners/config_scanner.py вҖ” Scan all AI client MCP config files
     3. scanners/process_scanner.py вҖ” Detect MCP processes via psutil
     4. scanners/network_scanner.py вҖ” Detect HTTP/SSE MCP servers via listener
     scanning
     5. scanners/workspace_scanner.py вҖ” Scan project-level .vscode/mcp.json,
     etc.
     6. scoring.py вҖ” Risk scoring (Low/Medium/High) based on approval status,
     credentials, external endpoints
     7. reporters/api_reporter.py вҖ” POST results to orchestrator /api/report
     8. reporters/file_reporter.py вҖ” Save local JSON reports
     9. cli.py вҖ” Typer CLI: agentwatch-agent scan, agentwatch-agent watch
     (continuous)

     Phase D: Dashboard

     1. Vite + React + Tailwind + TypeScript setup
     2. API client (fetch wrapper with JWT auth)
     3. WebSocket hook for real-time feed
     4. Layout with sidebar navigation
     5. Pages: Overview (stats), Live Feed, Agent Registry, Scan Results
     6. Dark theme (GitHub-style as in original)
     7. Build script outputs to orchestrator/app/static/

     Phase E: Containerization

     1. Orchestrator Dockerfile (multi-stage: dashboard build вҶ’ Python)
     2. Agent Dockerfile
     3. docker-compose.yml (orchestrator + PostgreSQL)

     Phase F: Helm Chart

     1. Chart.yaml with PostgreSQL dependency (Bitnami)
     2. values.yaml with all configurable settings
     3. Templates: Deployment, Service, Ingress, ConfigMap, Secret, HPA,
     ServiceAccount
     4. NOTES.txt with post-install instructions

     ---
     Key Design Decisions

     Authentication: Dual auth вҖ” JWT for human users (dashboard login), API keys
      for machine-to-machine (endpoint agents reporting). Both validated via
     FastAPI dependency injection.

     Audit Logging: Every API call that mutates state or executes commands logs
     to BOTH JSONL (backward compat) and PostgreSQL (queryable). Log entries
     always include: user_id, agent_id, session_id, action, timestamp,
     source_ip.

     Command Validation Fix: Strip single-quoted and double-quoted strings from
     command text before applying cmdlet regex pattern [A-Z][a-z]+-[A-Za-z]+.
     This prevents false positives on strings like "=== ACTIVE Global Admins 
     ===".

     Three-Lane Enforcement: Implemented as middleware вҖ” check agent registry
     status before routing to handler. Fast lane (approved) вҶ’ direct execution.
     Inspection lane (unknown) вҶ’ queue for review. Blocked lane вҶ’ 403.

     Cross-Platform Agent: Single Python codebase with platform.system()
     dispatch to OS-specific modules for path resolution and process inspection.
      No platform-specific dependencies.

     ---
     Verification Plan

     1. docker-compose up вҖ” starts orchestrator + PostgreSQL
     2. curl localhost:8000/api/health вҖ” health check responds
     3. Register a user, get JWT, use it on protected endpoints
     4. Create an agent via API, verify in registry
     5. Run endpoint agent locally: agentwatch-agent scan --orchestrator-url 
     http://localhost:8000
     6. Verify scan results appear in dashboard live feed
     7. helm template ./helm/agentwatch вҖ” validates chart renders
     8. Run pytest for orchestrator and agent test suites

       80 -## Known Issues in Existing Code                              
       65 +### Key Design Patterns                                       
       66  
       82 -1. **No user identity in logs** вҖ” agent and command logged, bu
          -t not who ran it.                                             
       83 -2. **No API authentication** вҖ” port 3000 is open to anyone on 
          -the network.                                                  
       84 -3. **Validation regex false positive** вҖ” pattern `[A-Z][a-z]+-
          -[A-Za-z]+` matches string literals inside commands (e.g., `"==
          -= ACTIVE Global Admins ==="`). Fix: strip quoted strings befor
          -e validation.                                                 
       85 -4. **CopilotBridge is voluntary** вҖ” developers who don't `Impo
          -rt-Module` are invisible (shadow agent problem).              
       86 -5. **AGENTS object hardcoded** вҖ” must externalize to database/
          -config with CRUD API.                                         
       87 -6. **Invoke-Expression in CopilotBridge** вҖ” executes arbitrary
          - strings; mitigated by blocked verb list but a security risk. 
       88 -7. **In-memory history** вҖ” resets on restart; must persist to 
          -database.                                                     
       67 +**Dual Auth**: JWT bearer tokens for human users (dashboard lo
          +gin), `aw_` prefixed API keys for machine-to-machine (endpoint
          + agents). Both validated via `app/auth.py:get_current_user` de
          +pendency.

вҸә Great observations. Three things to add:

  1. Runtime detection вҖ” docker containers vs npx/uvx vs native
  2. Local vs Remote classification вҖ” docker/localhost = local, external URLs =
  remote (exfiltration risk)
  3. AI client breakdown вҖ” which clients have MCP configs

  Let me update the config scanner, the scan model, and the dashboard.

вҸә Write(agent/agentwatch_agent/scanners/config_scanner.py)
  вҺҝ В Added 120 lines, removed 47 lines
       2  
       3  SECURITY PRINCIPLE: This scanner NEVER collects secrets, tokens
          , credentials,
       4  or any sensitive values. It only collects:
       5 -  - Server name                                                
       6 -  - Client name (which AI app)                                 
       7 -  - Transport type (stdio/sse/http)                            
       8 -  - Package name (the npm/pip/uvx package, NOT full command arg
         -s)                                                             
       9 -  - Endpoint URL (hostname + path only, auth headers/tokens str
         -ipped)                                                         
       5 +  - Server name, client name, transport type                   
       6 +  - Runtime (docker, npx, uvx, native)                         
       7 +  - Package name or container image (no tags with secrets)     
       8 +  - Endpoint URL (hostname + path only, auth stripped)         
       9 +  - Locality (local vs remote) for data exfiltration risk      
      10    - Env var NAMES (never values)
      11    - Whether credentials are present (boolean)
      12 +  - Container image version if available                       
      13  """
      14

     ...

      37 +    r"|secret[=:]\S+|authorization[=:]\S+|--header\s+\S+|--toke
         +n\s+\S+|--api-key\s+\S+)",

       64 +def _detect_runtime(server_cfg: dict[str, Any]) -> str:       
       65 +    """Detect the runtime: docker, npx, uvx, pip, or native.""
          +"                                                             
       66 +    command = server_cfg.get("command", "")                   
       67 +    runner = Path(command).name.lower() if command else ""    
       68 +    if runner == "docker":                                    
       69 +        return "docker"                                       
       70 +    if runner == "npx":                                       
       71 +        return "npx"                                          
       72 +    if runner in ("uvx", "uv"):                               
       73 +        return "uvx"                                          
       74 +    if runner in ("pip", "pipx"):                             
       75 +        return "pip"                                          
       76 +    return "native"                                           
       77 +                                                              
       78 +                                                              
       79 +def _extract_docker_image(server_cfg: dict[str, Any]) -> str |
          + None:                                                        
       80 +    """Extract Docker container image name from args. Strip re
          +gistry prefix for display."""                                 
       81 +    args = server_cfg.get("args", [])                         
       82 +    if not isinstance(args, list):                            
       83 +        return None                                           
       84 +                                                              
       85 +    # Docker image is typically the last non-flag arg, or afte
          +r "run" ... flags                                             
       86 +    # Pattern: docker run -i --rm -e FOO -e BAR <image>       
       87 +    # Skip flags (-i, --rm, -e and their values)              
       88 +    skip_next = False                                         
       89 +    for arg in args:                                          
       90 +        arg_str = str(arg)                                    
       91 +        if skip_next:                                         
       92 +            skip_next = False                                 
       93 +            continue                                          
       94 +        if arg_str in ("run", "-i", "--rm", "--init", "-t", "-
          +-tty"):                                                       
       95 +            continue                                          
       96 +        if arg_str == "-e":                                   
       97 +            skip_next = True                                  
       98 +            continue                                          
       99 +        if arg_str.startswith("-"):                           
      100 +            if "=" not in arg_str:                            
      101 +                skip_next = True                              
      102 +            continue                                          
      103 +        # This should be the image name                       
      104 +        # Could be: hosted.nexus.lordabbett.com/mcp/github/git
          +hub-mcp-server:0.28.1                                         
      105 +        # or: https://docker.io/docker.io/mcp/markitdown      
      106 +        image = arg_str.removeprefix("https://").removeprefix(
          +"http://")                                                    
      107 +        return image                                          
      108 +                                                              
      109 +    return None                                               
      110 +                                                              
      111 +                                                              
      112  def _extract_package_name(server_cfg: dict[str, Any]) -> str:
       65 -    """Extract just the package/binary name, not the full comm
          -and with args.                                                
      113 +    """Extract the package/binary name."""                    
      114 +    runtime = _detect_runtime(server_cfg)                     
      115  
       67 -    Examples:                                                 
       68 -      command=npx, args=["-y", "@modelcontextprotocol/server-g
          -ithub"]                                                       
       69 -        -> "@modelcontextprotocol/server-github"              
       70 -      command=uvx, args=["mcp-msdefenderkql"]                 
       71 -        -> "mcp-msdefenderkql"                                
       72 -      command=snyk, args=["mcp", "-t", "stdio"]

      176 +    """Classify as 'local' or 'remote'.

          +no external URL.

          +s)

вҸә Entered plan mode
  Claude is now exploring and designing an implementation approach.

вҸә Good question вҖ” this is a real technical challenge. Let me explain the options
   before planning.

  The core problem: MCP server tool lists aren't in static config files. The
  config files (mcp.json, claude_desktop_config.json) only contain server
  connection info (command, args, env vars). The actual tools are discovered at
  runtime via the MCP protocol вҖ” the client connects to the server and calls
  tools/list to get the tool catalog.

  Let me ask you a key question before designing the approach.
  вҺҝ В Tool use rejected

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· What would you like to clarify about the MCP tool discovery approaches? I
      can explain any of the three options in more detail, or if you have a 
     different idea for how to get tool lists, let me know. вҶ’ Explain how active
      probing works

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Here's how MCP tool discovery works under the hood. The MCP protocol uses
      JSON-RPC over stdio (or HTTP). When a client connects to a server, it 
     does:

     1. Client -> Server: `initialize` (handshake with capabilities)
     2. Server -> Client: response with server capabilities
     3. Client -> Server: `initialized` (confirmation)
     4. Client -> Server: `tools/list` (get all available tools)
     5. Server -> Client: array of tools with name, description, input schema

     The challenge: for STDIO servers (most of yours), the running process's 
     stdin/stdout is already owned by Claude Desktop/VS Code. We can't tap into 
     it.

     So the agent would need to START A TEMPORARY INSTANCE of each server, probe
      it, then shut it down. This is safe (read-only, ephemeral) but requires 
     the server binary to be available. It does NOT need credentials вҖ” most MCP 
     servers will start and return their tool list even without valid API keys 
     (auth only matters when you actually call a tool).

     For HTTP/SSE servers, we can probe the endpoint directly.

     Does this approach work for your environment? вҶ’ what are teh secueiy 
     implications of doing this? we have both stdio and http/sse

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Security implications breakdown:

     **STDIO probing (start temp process):**
     - Starts a NEW process on the endpoint (e.g., `npx 
     @modelcontextprotocol/server-github`)
     - Process runs for ~2-3 seconds, receives only initialize + tools/list, 
     then killed
     - NO credentials passed (env vars omitted intentionally) вҖ” server starts 
     but can't authenticate to backends
     - NO tool calls made вҖ” only tools/list (read the menu, don't order 
     anything)
     - Risk: minimal. The server binary is already installed and approved. 
     Starting it briefly without creds just reads its manifest
     - Concern: some servers might phone home on startup (check for updates, 
     telemetry). Mitigated by not passing env vars

     **HTTP/SSE probing:**
     - Connects to an already-running endpoint (e.g., 
     splunkcloud.com:8089/services/mcp)
     - Sends initialize + tools/list only
     - Risk: you're making a network request to an external service. But it's 
     the same service your MCP client already talks to
     - Concern: requires auth headers for most HTTP servers. Without them, the 
     probe will likely get a 401 and return no tools
     - For INTERNAL HTTP servers (on your network), this is low risk

     **Bottom line:** STDIO probing is actually SAFER than HTTP probing because 
     it's fully local and we control the process. HTTP probing touches the 
     network. I'd recommend STDIO probing for all configured servers, and skip 
     HTTP/SSE probing unless you explicitly opt in. Want to go with that? вҶ’ but 
     i dont want to give users those rights.. this needs to be controleld by 
     admins, and giving accesds to users makes it hard for us to do anything 
     from the security adn governance point of view

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· Understood вҖ” tool discovery should be admin-controlled, not 
     user-initiated. Here's the enterprise approach:

     The endpoint agent's scan behavior is controlled by **managed settings** 
     deployed via Intune/GPO (not by the user). The admin configures whether 
     tool discovery is enabled in the agent's config that gets pushed to 
     endpoints.

     When enabled, the agent automatically probes STDIO servers during its 
     scheduled scan, collects tool lists, and reports them to the orchestrator 
     alongside the regular scan data. Users don't run anything вҖ” the agent runs 
     as a scheduled task.

     In the dashboard, admins see a new "MCP Servers" tab showing every 
     discovered server with its full tool inventory. They can see which tools 
     each server exposes, what parameters they accept, and flag risky tools.

     The control flow:
     1. Admin deploys agent config via Intune/GPO with `discover_tools: true`
     2. Agent runs on schedule, scans configs, probes STDIO servers for tools
     3. Reports everything to orchestrator
     4. Dashboard shows full tool inventory per server

     Should I build this? вҶ’ Yes, build it with admin-managed config

вҸә Updated plan
  вҺҝ В /plan to preview

вҸә User approved Claude's plan
  вҺҝ В Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/snuggly-scribbling-toucan.md В· /plan to edit
     MCP Server Tool Discovery вҖ” Implementation Plan

     Context

     The user wants a new "MCP Servers" dashboard tab showing every discovered
     MCP server with its full tool inventory вҖ” what tools each server exposes,
     descriptions, and parameters. Tool discovery is admin-controlled via
     managed agent config (Intune/GPO), not user-initiated.

     How It Works

     Agent-side: MCP Tool Prober

     New scanner module: agent/agentwatch_agent/scanners/tool_prober.py

     For each STDIO MCP server found in config:
     1. Start a temp process using the same command/args from config (NO env
     vars вҖ” no creds)
     2. Send JSON-RPC over stdin: initialize вҶ’ wait for response вҶ’ initialized
     notification вҶ’ tools/list
     3. Capture tool names, descriptions, input schemas
     4. Kill the process (timeout: 5 seconds max)
     5. Return tool list per server

     Controlled by config flag discover_tools: true (default: false).

     For Docker-based servers: docker run --rm -i <image> with same probe flow.
     For HTTP/SSE servers: skip (would need auth).

     Agent config

     Add to CLI: --discover-tools flag on the scan command.
     In managed/enterprise deployment, this flag is set in the agent config
     pushed via Intune/GPO.

     API changes

     Update ScanReportRequest schema to accept tool data per config finding.
     Each config finding gets a new optional field: tools: list[dict] containing
      {name, description, input_schema}.

     New DB model: McpServer

     Deduplicated server registry built from scan data:
     - id, server_name, package, transport, runtime, locality
     - tools (JSON array of tool definitions)
     - clients (which AI clients have it configured)
     - endpoints (list of endpoints scanned on)
     - risk_level, has_credentials
     - first_seen, last_seen

     Populated/updated every time a scan report comes in. Deduplicates by
     server_name.

     Dashboard: new "MCP Servers" tab

     Route: /servers
     Shows a table of all unique MCP servers across all endpoints:
     - Server name, package, runtime (docker/npx/uvx), locality (local/remote)
     - Clients (VS Code, Claude Desktop, etc.)
     - Endpoints (which machines have it)
     - Tool count
     - Risk level, credentials flag

     Click a server вҶ’ expands to show:
     - Full tool list with name, description, input schema
     - Which endpoints have this server
     - Risk details

     Files to Create/Modify

     New files:

     - agent/agentwatch_agent/scanners/tool_prober.py вҖ” MCP protocol probe
     - orchestrator/app/models/mcp_server.py вҖ” McpServer model
     - orchestrator/app/routers/servers.py вҖ” CRUD endpoints for MCP servers
     - orchestrator/app/schemas/server.py вҖ” Pydantic schemas
     - dashboard/src/pages/Servers.tsx вҖ” New dashboard tab

     Modified files:

     - agent/agentwatch_agent/cli.py вҖ” Add --discover-tools flag
     - agent/agentwatch_agent/scanners/config_scanner.py вҖ” Attach tools to
     findings when probing enabled
     - orchestrator/app/routers/reports.py вҖ” On scan report, upsert McpServer
     records
     - orchestrator/app/models/__init__.py вҖ” Add McpServer import
     - orchestrator/app/main.py вҖ” Include servers router
     - dashboard/src/App.tsx вҖ” Add /servers route
     - dashboard/src/components/Layout.tsx вҖ” Add Servers nav item
     - dashboard/src/api/client.ts вҖ” Add getServers() method
     - dashboard/src/types/index.ts вҖ” Add McpServer type

     Verification

     1. agentwatch-agent scan --discover-tools --orchestrator-url 
     http://localhost:8000 --api-key ...
     2. Check that tool lists appear in scan report
     3. Check /api/servers returns deduplicated server list with tools
     4. Dashboard /servers tab shows servers with expandable tool inventory

вқҜ a few things i noticed... some mcp servers have no tools-- specifucally       
remote ones.. is that intentional coz we are using creds to probe?              

вҸә Yes, exactly. The prober intentionally skips HTTP/SSE servers (the remote ones
   like io.github.github/github-mcp-server, makenotion/notion-mcp-server,
  com.postman/postman-mcp-server) because they need auth headers to connect. And
   for STDIO servers like snyk and splunk-mcp-server, the probe either timed out
   or the server errored without credentials.

  The 0-tool servers break down into:
